## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration arises from nonlinear restoring forces in x, possible nonlinear damping in v, and potential external driving forces periodic in t.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force with linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic nonlinearity plus damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced cubic oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring with damping)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2)**(-1) (rational restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (nonlinear damping and restoring)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving force)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v**2 (energy-dependent restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use when oscillation is symmetric
- Even-power terms (x**2) in restoring force indicate asymmetric potential wells — use when oscillation amplitude differs in positive vs negative direction
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - c*x**2)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (self-excitation or limit cycles, as in Van der Pol)
- Sinusoidal position dependence sin(c*x) indicates a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum) rather than polynomial approximation
- Cubic restoring force x**3 with same sign as linear term x indicates hardening spring; opposite sign indicates softening spring
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests autonomous/conservative system; presence of sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving
- Products x*v or x**2*v indicate nonlinear energy exchange between kinetic and potential modes
- Rational forms like x/(1 + c*x**2) can model bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements
